  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_a4a06c8d-172e-481e-b839-923970a87055'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"
      loadScript(APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL, initAppleId);
    };

<span id="freeTextContainer3439706821436724357">Everybody knows Cate Cahill and her sisters are eccentric. Too pretty, too reclusive, and far too educated for their own good.   <span id="freeText3439706821436724357" style="display:none">Everybody knows Cate Cahill and her sisters are eccentric. Too pretty, too reclusive, and far too educated for their own good. But the truth is even worse: they’re witches. And if their secret is discovered by the priests of the Brotherhood, it would mean an asylum, a prison ship—or an early grave.<br /><br />Before her mother died, Cate promised to protect her sisters. But with only six months left to choose between marriage and the Sisterhood, she might not be able to keep her word... especially after she finds her mother’s diary, uncovering a secret that could spell her family’s destruction. Desperate to find alternatives to their fate, Cate starts scouring banned books and questioning rebellious new friends, all while juggling tea parties, shocking marriage proposals, and a forbidden romance with the completely unsuitable Finn Belastra.<br /><br />If what her mother wrote is true, the Cahill girls aren’t safe. Not from the Brotherhood, the Sisterhood—not even from each other.</span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies" href="/user/show/4527753-khanh-first-of-her-name-mother-of-bunnies">Khanh, first of her name, mother of bunnies</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer944412798" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer657058954826802905"><b>Actual rating: 3.5. Rounded down for the pointless motherfucking love triangle.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Mother didn’t trust Father to fight for us. Truth be told, she didn’t do a very good job of it herself. She left me with a diary full of cryptic warnings and a responsibility that should have been hers.<br/>I will keep my sisters safe...while I have breath left in my body.</i>
</blockquote>I'm an idiot. This is what I get for not reading the summary. For some fucking reason, I thought this was an adult novel. It's not. I thought it was </span>
  <span id="freeText657058954826802905" style="display:none"><b>Actual rating: 3.5. Rounded down for the pointless motherfucking love triangle.</b><blockquote>
  <i>Mother didn’t trust Father to fight for us. Truth be told, she didn’t do a very good job of it herself. She left me with a diary full of cryptic warnings and a responsibility that should have been hers.<br />I will keep my sisters safe...while I have breath left in my body.</i>
</blockquote>I'm an idiot. This is what I get for not reading the summary. For some fucking reason, I thought this was an adult novel. It's not. I thought it was magical realism. It's not, it's about witches. I thought it takes place in the modern US. It doesn't. Then I thought it took place in 18th century US. That ended quickly when I encountered a family named the Ishidas (there weren't a whole lot of Japanese people in the US in the 18th century, ok?). This book is <b>an alternate history of the US with a Puritan-like religious sect called "The Brotherhood" in charge, in which witches existed and are persecuted</b>.<br /><br />So now that we've finished discussing how dumb I am for not paying attention to the summary, let's discuss the book itself:<br /><br /><u>The not-so-good</u>:<br />- <b>Completely fucking pointless love triangle</b>: what's better than one awesome guy?! Two of them! WHY?!<br /><br />- <b>I-don't-want-to-be-a-witch syndrone</b>: the main character suffers from it.<br /><br />- <b>The length</b>: It's a long book, and there is a decided lack of action. This is an alternate history of the 1900s US, expect plenty of courtship and tea parties with your witchcraft.<br /><br /><u>The good:</u><br /><br />- <b>Surprisingly feminist</b>: there's a big message about female empowerment, education, and oppression in this book.<br /><br />- <b>A likeable main character who doesn't feel like a Mary Sue</b>: she is not a pretty pretty pretty girl like the summary tells you. She's dowdy, she's awkward, and she's more a mother hen than a peacock.<br /><br />- <b>An interesting, if initially confusing-as-fuck alternate history</b>: once you get that figured out, we're golden.<br /><br />- <b>Diversity</b>: people of color. Lesbians. A tongue-in-cheek reference to how liberal the alternate Middle-Eastern countries are in comparison. The witches themselves are believed and abhorred by the Brotherhood for being women who live with other women, and it's implied that they're lesbians. They're not, but it's the prejudice.<br /><br />- <b>Interesting and unexpected side characters</b>: you think a character is a stupid trope? Nope!<br /><br />- <b>A well-drawn sisterly relationship</b>: this is a book about sisters, and it shows.<br /><br /><u>The Summary</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>You must watch over your sisters for me. Keep them safe. There’s so much I wanted to tell you. And now I haven’t time.</i>
</blockquote>Contrary to the fucking summary, 16-year-old <b>Cate Cahill</b> isn't "too pretty." She's the rather dowdy oldest sister to her younger siblings, Tess, 12, and Maura, 15. Her mother passed away when she was 13, leaving her with a cryptic message and a mission to watch over her sisters.<br /><br />It's a pretty important mission, because <b>the Cahill sisters have a secret: they're witches.</b> Not even their despondent, grieving shadow of a father knows. It's a secret that could kill them because they live in an alternate version of circa 1900 United States. This US is ruled by The Brotherhood, a fanatical religious sect that doesn't believe in the rights of women. This is because <b>over 100 years ago, they defeated the witches, women said to be powerful, wicked, evil, lustful.</b> They are kept controlled, regardless of their lack of magic.<blockquote>
  <i>The Brothers are afraid the witches will rise up again someday, Mother said, so they loathe the idea of powerful women. We are not permitted to study and go to university as men do, or to take up professions.</i>
</blockquote>Since then, the Brotherhood has led <b>a reign of purity, chastity, where women are subdued and submissive.</b><blockquote>
  <i>The message is clear: women who are too opinionated or too educated, too odd or too curious, are punished. They deserve whatever fate they get.<br />Women like us.</i>
</blockquote>Women are evil. Magic is reviled. The Cahill sisters are witches who must practice their witchcraft in secret, and they hate it. Spirited Tessa cannot help using spells where she shouldn't. Fiery Maura wants the freedom to practice her witchcraft---she doesn't feel like magic is something of which they should be ashamed.<blockquote>
  <i>“We’re witches, Cate. We were born that way. Magic isn’t shameful, no matter what the Brothers would have us believe. It’s a gift. I wish you would accept that.”</i>
</blockquote><b>Whereas Cate worries all the time, and wishes she weren't a witch.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I frown at my reflection in the pond, wishing with every fiber of my being that I weren’t a witch.</i>
</blockquote>Cate and her sisters are of marrying age, and a conniving neighbor with the aspiration of being the next Mrs. Cahill has convinced their dad to get them a governess---a dour Sister. A convent-like organization for women who don't marry. Cate and her sisters aren't fond of the idea...that's one more person they have to keep their secret from, but <b>this governess isn't the plain sourpuss of a nun they expected.</b> She is young, she is beautiful, she is fashiomable...<blockquote>
  <i>Sister Elena is pretty—no, beautiful—with smooth brown skin and black ringlets peeking out from beneath her hood. And she’s fashionable—as fashionable as the Brothers’ strictures will allow. Her dress has a wide bell skirt in a soft pink that reminds me of Mother’s peonies. </i>
</blockquote>And she may just be the ally that they need.<br /><br />Cate has more on her mind than just the secrecy of her magic, she's of an age to marry, and <b>for girls like her, there are only two choices once she turns 17: marry, or become a sister.</b> Will she be marrying her childhood sweetheart, <b>Paul</b>...who understands her.<blockquote>
  <i>“A life with you will never be dull, will it, and that’s just what I want. Think about it, Cate. That’s all I ask. Can you do that?”</i>
</blockquote>Or the mysterious <b>Finn</b>.<blockquote>
  <i>Finn squares his shoulders—which have gotten a good deal sturdier since the last time I saw him. Or paid attention, at any rate. How long has it been since I actually looked? He’s gotten awfully handsome; it can’t have happened overnight.</i>
</blockquote>Adding to her headaches is her mother's mysterious message, it seems like <b>Cate and her sister are in danger</b>. There is a prophecy---will they be the one to fulfil it? Hell, will they live long enough to see it?<blockquote>
  <i>...if the Brothers found out, they would kill me. Immediately and without trial. Perhaps they’d make an example of all three of us—burn us at the stake, or hang us in the town square, the way they did in Great-Grandmother’s day.</i>
</blockquote><u>The Setting</u>: Whaaa?! This book was really, really confusing at first. I thought it was historical US, it's not. It's an alternate version of the US, where witchcraft exists and is stifled for fear. Around 100 years ago, the Brotherhood gained power. They killed all the witches, they set up a Puritan-like regime under which women aren't allowed access to higher education (some Brethren don't believe women should read at all) and should be <b>submissive to men at all times.</b> They use the witches' power to justify suppressing young women and making them subservient.<blockquote>
  <i>They cared nothing for protecting girls’ virtue. They would have women aping men— dressing immodestly, running businesses, even forgoing marriage to live in unnatural unions with other women.”</i>
</blockquote><b>This book has a lot of diversity.</b> There are Japanese families and side characters. The governess has "brown skin." There are lesbians, it is implied that some of the witches are lesbians.<br /><br />Furthermore, with the Middle Eastern circumstance these days where women are denied access to education---this book makes a <b>tongue-in-cheek reference to the liberalness of the Middle Eastern countries compared to the US in this alternate universe.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I hold back a sigh. What I wouldn’t give to share in the freedoms of Arab girls. They’re allowed to inherit property and go to university; they’ve even been given the right to vote.</i>
</blockquote>Overall, I felt like the world building was very well-done, if confusing at first.<br /><br /><u>Cate</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>I hate that I’ve taken this small happiness away from her. When I was her age, I liked to run through the gardens, and I suppose I was careless with my magic, too. Now I have to play mother for Tess and Maura, and ignore the wild girl that still bangs in my heart, begging to be let out.</i>
</blockquote><b>A really sympathetic character.</b> She is a girl who is forced to grow old before her time. She has to play disciplinarian to her two contrary, wilder, free-spirited sister, and it sucks the life out of her to do so. There is no question that the sisters love one another, and Cate feels her responsibility heavy on her shoulders. <b>She is prepared to give up her own happiness to keep them safe.</b><blockquote>
  <i>It’s been years since I’ve let myself consider what I want. It hardly matters. I didn’t want Mother to die; I didn’t want Father to turn into a shadow of his old self; I didn’t want the responsibility of policing my sisters. I certainly never wanted to be a witch in the first place.<br />The universe has yet to take my wishes under consideration.</i>
</blockquote>I love her occasional moments of anger and resentment at having been forced to grow up so fast, so soon.<blockquote>
  <i>It’s rare that I’ve let myself feel angry with Mother. She’s dead; she can’t defend herself. But now I’m shaking with it. How could she? How could she die and leave me here to deal with all of this alone?</i>
</blockquote><b>What I didn't like about Cate was her hatred of her own powers.</b> She has an unique power, and no, she doesn't feel like a Mary Sue. Cate believes her witchcraft wicked, she hates her powers, she thinks herself evil. I don't like that. If I had powers, even if they were presecuted, I'd revel in it. Find a way to work it to my advantage. Don't be a motherfucking pussy. EMBRACE THE POWER. Cate sometimes feel week because of her own denial, and I didn't appreciate that character flaw, especially when power is something I would so embrace.<u>The Romance</u>: <blockquote>
  <i>I want to chase right after Finn. I don’t care how big a fool I’d look.<br />But I can’t. I’d be no better than that Penelope. Paul’s just proposed; I can’t go chasing after another man, one who may not even want me.</i>
</blockquote><b>Why?! Fucking why?!</b> Paul is PERFECT. Here we have a case of a completely needless love triangle. She has her childhood best friend, Paul, with whom she has an <i>understanding</i>, which means that everyone in the 'hood knows they will get married one day, and she knows it, and Paul knows it, except BOOM, OUT OF THE BLUE COMES FUCKING FINN. Who takes all the Funn out of things. Sorry, couldn't resist.<br /><br />Paul is so nice. He understands Cate so well. They get along so well.<blockquote>
  <i>“Because we’re alike, you and I. We want adventures, not quiet nights at home by the fire. I think I could make you happy if you’d let me.” Paul’s voice goes gravelly, and he takes both my hands in his. </i>
</blockquote>Which is why I don't fucking understand the need for a love triangle at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="657058954826802905" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer180339665" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer17062318564785085149">Well, I read the first 150 pages of this novel and then skimmed another 50, but this one just isn't holding my attention, I'm afraid. The writing and mood are actually rather nice, and the language seems pretty appropriate to early 20th century New England (albeit an alternate history version) aside from some jarring words here and there. <br/><br/>There just isn't enough witchery in this book for me, however, since the book seems very heavily centered around the romance. And unfortunately, the romance wa</span>
  <span id="freeText17062318564785085149" style="display:none">Well, I read the first 150 pages of this novel and then skimmed another 50, but this one just isn't holding my attention, I'm afraid. The writing and mood are actually rather nice, and the language seems pretty appropriate to early 20th century New England (albeit an alternate history version) aside from some jarring words here and there. <br /><br />There just isn't enough witchery in this book for me, however, since the book seems very heavily centered around the romance. And unfortunately, the romance wasn't very compelling to me either, as the two boys--and Cate herself--do very little that is truly interesting or remarkable. And please, spare us from any more found-diaries-as-plot-device machinations!<br /><br />Still, I expect this might be more appealing to lovers of YA historical romance who don't mind that the paranormal elements take a back seat, which is why <a href="http://backinthemidnightgarden.blogspot.com/2012/01/giveaway-alert-born-wicked.html" rel="nofollow noopener">I'm giving away my copy</a> if you're interested in trying out the book for yourself! The book, which is the first in a planned trilogy, will be released next month in February 2012.</span>
  <a data-text-id="17062318564785085149" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_229739646" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/229739646" />
    <a title="Tatiana" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana"><img alt="Tatiana" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1249783659p2/2250020.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/229739646?book_show_action=true">Nov 01, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tatiana" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tatiana" href="/user/show/2250020-tatiana">Tatiana</a>
      </span>

          marked it as dnf




        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=urban-fantasy">urban-fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2250020-tatiana?shelf=why-the-hype">why-the-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer229739646" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11107100086302149256">Whatever I am going to write here will probably sound hypocritical in the light of the recent ramblings about genre/commercial/popular (whatever you want to call it) fiction that I started in my <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days__1_' title='Angelfall (Penryn & the End of Days #1) by Susan Ee' rel='nofollow noopener'>Angelfall</a> and <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11594257.Under_the_Never_Sky' title='Under the Never Sky by Veronica Rossi' rel='nofollow noopener'>Under the Never Sky</a> reviews, but here it is. <br/><br/>I've only read a couple of chapters of <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11715276.Born_Wicked__The_Cahill_Witch_Chronicles___1_' title='Born Wicked (The Cahill Witch Chronicles, #1) by Jessica Spotswood' rel='nofollow noopener'>Born Wicked</a> and thus far there are no objective issues with this novel that would justify my giving it a low rating or a bad review. It is written like everything else popular in YA right now, down to the 1s</span>
  <span id="freeText11107100086302149256" style="display:none">Whatever I am going to write here will probably sound hypocritical in the light of the recent ramblings about genre/commercial/popular (whatever you want to call it) fiction that I started in my <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11500217.Angelfall__Penryn___the_End_of_Days__1_" title="Angelfall (Penryn &amp; the End of Days #1) by Susan Ee" rel="nofollow noopener">Angelfall</a> and <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11594257.Under_the_Never_Sky" title="Under the Never Sky by Veronica Rossi" rel="nofollow noopener">Under the Never Sky</a> reviews, but here it is. <br /><br />I've only read a couple of chapters of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11715276.Born_Wicked__The_Cahill_Witch_Chronicles___1_" title="Born Wicked (The Cahill Witch Chronicles, #1) by Jessica Spotswood" rel="nofollow noopener">Born Wicked</a> and thus far there are no objective issues with this novel that would justify my giving it a low rating or a bad review. It is written like everything else popular in YA right now, down to the 1st person present tense narration; a teen girl protagonist who is smart and protective of her family, who is forced to fight against the social system that oppresses her, who strives for independence and freedom; a love interest/love triangle introduced at the very beginning. I can't accuse <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11715276.Born_Wicked__The_Cahill_Witch_Chronicles___1_" title="Born Wicked (The Cahill Witch Chronicles, #1) by Jessica Spotswood" rel="nofollow noopener">Born Wicked</a> of anything but it being a standard write-by-numbers commercial fare and its failure to entertain me. And if I am not entertained while reading something this formulaic, everything falls apart - the characters seem like cliches, the plot predictable, and the world-building nonsensical. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11715276.Born_Wicked__The_Cahill_Witch_Chronicles___1_" title="Born Wicked (The Cahill Witch Chronicles, #1) by Jessica Spotswood" rel="nofollow noopener">Born Wicked</a> is marketed as a <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/3682.A_Great_and_Terrible_Beauty__Gemma_Doyle___1_" title="A Great and Terrible Beauty (Gemma Doyle, #1) by Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">A Great and Terrible Beauty</a> stand-in, but as flawed as <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/2526.Libba_Bray" title="Libba Bray" rel="nofollow noopener">Libba Bray</a>'s Gemma Doyle trilogy was, it was never this... glaringly uninteresting and unoriginal.<br /><br />It goes without saying, this book might entertain someone else.</span>
  <a data-text-id="11107100086302149256" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="friendReviews elementListBrown" >
    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1072611347" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1072611347" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1072611347?book_show_action=true">Oct 05, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=witches">witches</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=family">family</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=love-triangle">love-triangle</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=sisterhood">sisterhood</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=religion">religion</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=secrets">secrets</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1072611347" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12371433247432941051"><b>*2.5 stars*</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412531454i/11387270._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='200' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Cate is sixteen. Three months before her seventeenth birthday, she has to choose, at the intention ceremony, if she’s going to marry or join the Sisterhood.<br/><br/>What is the Sisterhood?<br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>The Sisters are the feminine arm of the Brotherhood, only without any power: they do not preside over legal disputes, or create addendums to the morality code, or judge the cases of girls accused of witchery. They live isolated in convents in the cities and dedicate their lives in service to the Lord, educ</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText12371433247432941051" style="display:none"><b>*2.5 stars*</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1412531454i/11387270._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Cate is sixteen. Three months before her seventeenth birthday, she has to choose, at the intention ceremony, if she’s going to marry or join the Sisterhood.<br><br>What is the Sisterhood?<br><br><b>
  <blockquote>The Sisters are the feminine arm of the Brotherhood, only without any power: they do not preside over legal disputes, or create addendums to the morality code, or judge the cases of girls accused of witchery. They live isolated in convents in the cities and dedicate their lives in service to the Lord, educating girls in their elite boarding schools, occasionally serving as governess.<br>
</blockquote>
</b><br>Cate does not want to join them. She promised to take care of her sisters, Maura and Tess, and how could she do so, while being in New London?<br><br>The story takes place in 1900 in New England, a place where witches are either sentenced to the prison ship or the madhouse. Let’s say that they don’t want to be discovered and live in secrecy. <br><br>She could marry…that would be the wisest choice. But to whom? There’s Paul, the childhood friend in love with her. And there's Finn, their new gardener whom she comes to appreciate…very very much. Why? I have no idea. Sure, he’s sweet and gentle but, to be honest, I found him normal and pretty boring. Nothing special. Same goes for Paul, actually. Needless to say, I did not care for the romance.<br><br>Cate is a good character and how much she cares for her sisters is admirable. I wish we had seen more of Tess, the younger sister, though. She seems to be present mostly at the beginning and then not so much anymore. Maura, her, is and that's great except for the fact that she and Cate don’t have the best of relationships.<br><br>The plot had potential but there wasn’t enough magic, in my opinion. I believe it’s mostly because they have to hind it but, still, a story with witches needs witchery! <br><br>And, the pacing, it was too slow. There isn't much happening in the plot and so there are some parts that drag or feel like fillers.<br><br>The writing was good enough but there was nothing different, from the majority of YA books, in it. It didn’t impress me but it was pleasant enough to read.<br><br>I believe the sequel may be better, since I thought the ending was interesting and gives a lot of possibilities. I will read it, but it certainly will not be a priority.<br><br>If you want to read a story filled with magic and exciting romance, this may not be the perfect choice but, if you want to read a story containing family as one of the themes, some cute romance and an historical setting, this is it.<br><br></span>
  <a data-text-id="12371433247432941051" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154540761" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154540761?book_show_action=true">Mar 15, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Kenneally" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Kenneally" href="/user/show/3735982-miranda-kenneally">Miranda Kenneally</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154540761" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7887738170759185767">This book is one you can't miss. I'm already dying to know what happens in books 2 and 3! <br/><br/>Jessica Spotswood is an enormously talented author whose prose is gorgeous and full and lush and makes me want to live in the world she's created, an alternate history of America in the 1890s. The author's style reminds me of Kristin Cashore's -- the imagery made me want to attend the tea parties and wear the dresses and hang out in the gardens. I seriously loved this book, and had a hard time putting it do</span>
  <span id="freeText7887738170759185767" style="display:none">This book is one you can't miss. I'm already dying to know what happens in books 2 and 3! <br /><br />Jessica Spotswood is an enormously talented author whose prose is gorgeous and full and lush and makes me want to live in the world she's created, an alternate history of America in the 1890s. The author's style reminds me of Kristin Cashore's -- the imagery made me want to attend the tea parties and wear the dresses and hang out in the gardens. I seriously loved this book, and had a hard time putting it down, constantly wanting to return to it. And did I mention there's kissing? There's lots of it! And it's yummy! <br /><br />The main character, Cate, is a strong YA heroine who I loved rooting for. So many people depend on her and I can't see how Cate doesn't buckle under the pressure, but she shines through it all because she's so strong and loving. She cares deeply about her family. It's easy to relate to Cate because she has such strong desires that she wants to pursue, but has to juggle taking care of her family at the same time. She knows how to look at situations from all angles. The characters are all wonderfully drawn, especially Cate's younger sisters, Maura and Tess, and the bookshop owner, Mrs. Belastra.<br /><br />I'm not saying anything about the plot except for that it's super engaging. <br /><br />I can't wait to see what happens in the next book!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7887738170759185767" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_182500195" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/182500195" />
    <a title="Kristi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi"><img alt="Kristi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1496094866p2/1310688.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/182500195?book_show_action=true">Jul 06, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kristi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kristi" href="/user/show/1310688-kristi">Kristi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer182500195" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer15920470450656244209">Poor Cate. This girl has far too much responsibility. She takes care of the household as well as her two younger sisters. On top of that she has to keep hidden the fact that all three girls are witches, less they be persecuted. Cate seems to be lost after the death of her mother and her father isn’t much help since he is often absent from the girls lives. I just wanted to bundle this girl up in a hug and tell her everything was going to be okay. Though I’m not sure that would have been the truth</span>
  <span id="freeText15920470450656244209" style="display:none">Poor Cate. This girl has far too much responsibility. She takes care of the household as well as her two younger sisters. On top of that she has to keep hidden the fact that all three girls are witches, less they be persecuted. Cate seems to be lost after the death of her mother and her father isn’t much help since he is often absent from the girls lives. I just wanted to bundle this girl up in a hug and tell her everything was going to be okay. Though I’m not sure that would have been the truth.<br /><br />In addition to hiding her secret from the world, it seems as though her mother was keeping secrets from Cate as well. Ones that she doesn’t discover until after her mother’s death and upon the arrival of a mysterious letter. Cate works to discover her mother’s secrets and finds love in the process. But don’t expect a happily every after. This one exits with one of “those” endings! I am DYING for book two.<br /><br />It took me a while to read this book. Not because I didn’t like the book, because I adored this book. Jessica Spotswood is a wonderful writing. It was a beautifully written story! So enchanting. I had a hard time reading this book because I was going through a very stressful situation with my life at the time and I had a hard time concentrating on this novel. There is so much that happens in this story, so many obstacles and all I wanted was a happy ending! So, I took a break and waited until I could give this book the attention it deserved and then I didn’t look back!<br /><br />There were a lot of obstacles in this story, and I wish I could have helped Cate overcome them. I grew to admire her tenacity and her protection of her younger sisters. She is so selfless at times, I just wanted her to do something for herself, just once! This book is the definition of emotional roller-coaster!<br /><br />I so enjoyed the love story. I’m always a sucker for a story with a love element. What can I say? I love that feeling of falling in love! And Born Wicked has a somewhat complicated love story. Does Cate belong with the childhood friend that’s always been there for her, or the boy that seems to have insight into her very soul. I know who I am rooting for. I can’t fail to mention that closet scene…. whew! I just wanted to stand up and cheer!<br /><br />I can’t wait to see where this story goes and how the prophecy unfolds! Loved the world, loved the characters, loved the writing! And that cover is gorgeous too, isn’t it!?!?</span>
  <a data-text-id="15920470450656244209" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_289025284" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/289025284" />
    <a title="Ari" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3564852-ari"><img alt="Ari" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1451393828p2/3564852.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/289025284?book_show_action=true">Mar 05, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Ari" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Ari" href="/user/show/3564852-ari">Ari</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=2012">2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3564852-ari?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer289025284" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3906034188322871894">Lovely!<br/><a href='http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jessica-spotswood/review-born-wicked.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371556i/724678.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>This is bit of a magical story about witches in a very difficult time - when they are hunted down, when they have to hide, to pretend to be ‘normal’ and not draw any attention to them. It's a story about a young girl that needs to protect herself and her sisters from all the dangers that might break them apart, a story about young love and old prophecies, and everything in between.<br/><br/><strong>THE COVER</strong><br/>... isn't it beautiful? I mean, I am not sure of the relationship with the book, as the girl’s d</span>
  <span id="freeText3906034188322871894" style="display:none">Lovely!<br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jessica-spotswood/review-born-wicked.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371556i/724678.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>This is bit of a magical story about witches in a very difficult time - when they are hunted down, when they have to hide, to pretend to be ‘normal’ and not draw any attention to them. It's a story about a young girl that needs to protect herself and her sisters from all the dangers that might break them apart, a story about young love and old prophecies, and everything in between.<br><br><strong>THE COVER</strong><br>... isn't it beautiful? I mean, I am not sure of the relationship with the book, as the girl’s dress doesn’t match the era from the story, but I think it's beautiful nevertheless. From the very first time I saw it I knew I wanted to read this book and I was more than happy to see how much I liked it.<br><br><strong>THE CHARACTERS</strong><br><br><strong> Cate </strong><br>The story is told from Cate's point a view. She is a young lady that has to watch over her sisters (Tess and Maura, both younger than Cate), all of them being witches, but not all of them being OK with the fact that they have to hide their powers. Cate needs to make a decision in order to keep her sisters safe; she needs to decide her future and maybe theirs as well.<br><br><strong>Her sisters</strong><br>The sweet an obedient<em> Tess</em> is the youngest and, even though she barely got her powers, she is really talented. I liked the relationship between her and Cate – they helped and understood each other and there wasn’t anything in the whole world that they wouldn’t do to protect the other.<br><em>Maura</em> is a bit different – she is more rebellious, she doesn’t like to take orders and she is proud of being a witch (as she doesn't see it like a curse at all). She wants to know more about what she could do with the power of her mind and she doesn't want to waste this gift by hiding.<br><br>I loved the family dynamics, with a bit of jealousy and some fights. It showed that even though it wasn’t the perfect family, they still loved each other; that even though they didn’t agree with what they had to do, they still tried to protect each other no matter what.<br><br><strong><a href="http://mysticallair.deviantart.com/art/Chapter-4-God-Sent-34959813" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371556i/724679.jpg" alt="" width="300" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><br>The mother</strong><br>There where many things I wondered when it came to the mother. The first one is why didn’t she give Cate more advices, why didn’t she help her in any way she could. You might say that the journal was enough but it wasn’t. It was this big mystery that couldn’t be uncovered properly.<br>Also, why the insistence to have another baby and risk her life, leaving her daughters unprotected? She didn’t trust her husband enough and I am not sure how much love could have been between them, so I just hope the reason was good enough to be worth dying for.<br><br><strong>The father</strong><br>He was mostly absent so I didn’t get what was his role in the story. I resented him for being so clueless and for not caring about his own daughters and I resented the way Tess was suffering because of the lack of affection from his part.<br><br><strong>THE LOVE STORY</strong><br>Love is a big part of the story but the heroine had her priorities straight. She put her sisters first no matter what; she was selfless and would sacrifice everything for her sisters.<br><br><a href="http://www.wallpaperfox.com/download/274-Born-from-the-fountain-of-love-1024x768" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380371556i/724680.jpg" alt="" width="300" height="225" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>You know how I don’t enjoy <em>love triangles </em>but in this case it worked just fine. I mean, Cate's heart belongs to only one guy; the problem was that he was not ‘good enough’ in the eyes of the society she was living in.<br>It was a tough decision for her to make as both guys seemed to care about her, to understand her in some way, both guys wanted to make her happy. But happiness is hard to be achieved when it depends on too many people, in fact when it depends on the others and not on yourself.<br><br>Now that I think about this, I guess I wanted more time with the boys, to get to know them better, because this part of the story was a bit rushed. But there were some cute scenes involving the 3 of them (together or not) and I found myself smiling a lot and caring about Cate's decisions.<br>Also there were some big mistakes that she made and I can’t wait to see how will those affect the action in the second book.<br><br><strong>THE WORLD SETTLING </strong><br>I loved this ‘New England’ with the Brotherhood so controlling and the Sisterhood a bit mysterious in it’s acts. I loved to read about the prophecy, about how one of the 3 sisters might change history, and I love to read stories from the 19th century, as (like I said) there is something magical about that period. I still wonder why the Brothers didn’t come for Cate or her sisters like they did with other girls (was it because of their father, or was it in their plans to do it in the future?), but as I see things now, I am not sure if I’ll get my answer.<br><br><strong>THE ENDING</strong><br>I can’t say that I didn’t see it coming somehow, as everything that happened pointed to that direction, but there were some things that took my by surprise. It is a bit of a cliffhanger and it made me want to wish for the next book to be published really, really soon.<br><br>I hope you will enjoy this book as well. Happy midnight reading everyone!<br><br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jessica-spotswood/review-born-wicked.html" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380313075i/688704.jpg" alt="" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><i>This review can also be found at <a title="ReadingAfterMidnight" href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/jessica-spotswood/review-born-wicked.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">ReadingAfterMidnight.com</a></i><br>____________________________________________<br><br><a href="http://www.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (EN)</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/readingaftermidnight" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/lil_aree" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="http://readingaftermidnight.tumblr.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Tumblr</a> |<a href="http://www.bloglovin.com/en/blog/3285482/reading-after-midnight/" rel="nofollow noopener"> Bloglovin'</a> | <a href="http://ro.readingaftermidnight.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog (RO)</a><br>____________________________________________<br></span>

    <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland"><img alt="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1417030210p2/5749698.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/378960803?book_show_action=true">Jul 28, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Kat (Lost in Neverland)" href="/user/show/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland">Kat (Lost in Neverland)</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=boring-as-shit">boring-as-shit</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=cheesy-romance">cheesy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=stupid-heroine">stupid-heroine</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5749698-kat-lost-in-neverland?shelf=lust-and-love-are-not-the-same">lust-and-love-are-not-the-same</a>,

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer378960803" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer34449398762557790">I met the author and got a copy signed. She's really sweet and genuine, and sounds a lot like me. <br/><br/><b>After Finishing</b><br/><br/>Unfortunately, I was immensely disappointed with this book. I especially despised the ending. This was such an obvious attempt to make a series, it's not even...UGH. <br/><br/>2.5 Stars<br/><br/>Cate and her two sisters are witches. They strive to keep their secret from the strict, religious Brotherhood who they have to display obedience to, despite their hatred toward witches and women alike. <br/>In a few m</span>
  <span id="freeText34449398762557790" style="display:none">I met the author and got a copy signed. She's really sweet and genuine, and sounds a lot like me. <br><br><b>After Finishing</b><br><br>Unfortunately, I was immensely disappointed with this book. I especially despised the ending. This was such an obvious attempt to make a series, it's not even...UGH. <br><br>2.5 Stars<br><br>Cate and her two sisters are witches. They strive to keep their secret from the strict, religious Brotherhood who they have to display obedience to, despite their hatred toward witches and women alike. <br>In a few months, Cate must either choose a husband or have the Brotherhood choose one for her. Or, of course, the other option is to join the Sisterhood, a religious convent in New England. But how could a witch be part of the Sisterhood? Cate doesn't believe it safe.<br>Everyone expects her to choose Paul, a childhood friend who has returned from New England to propose to her. But her true feelings lie in Finn, their bookish gardener. <br><br>Cate must protect her sisters at all costs, and as more secrets from her mother and godmother's past start to unravel, everything is going to change for the worse. <br><br><br>This was me throughout most of the book;<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380385639ra/744673.gif" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I was mind-bogglingly bored for almost the entire story. It was an average Jane Austen novel, I'll tell you that. But with way more 'lovey dovey' 'kissy kissy' cliche romance scenes. <br>Why are the romance scenes cliche, you ask? Examples;<br><br>1. Finn gets wounded and Cate acts as his nurse and heals his wounds. We've all seen it before. And, <i>of course</i>, Cate has to be all blushy as she imagines what he looks like under his clothes. <br><br>2. The clumsy Cate trips and Finn romantically catches her and pulls her against him. <br>*major eye rolling* <br><br>3. There's bloody love triangle, for crying out loud. Though, okay, she doesn't feel anything for Paul, so it's a one-sided love triangle. Still. <br><br><br>I've heard a lot of people either rave or complain about the ending. I must say I am part of the latter group. <br>It was so obviously a trick to make this book into a series, even though Jessica could have easily fit the entire series into one book, wrapping it up quite nicely. Considering how bland, slow paced, with generally no action, and boring the book was, it would have been an improvement.<br><br>I liked Finn. He was a bookish guy with glasses, and you all know how I <i>love</i> my bookish boys with glasses. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380385639i/744674.jpg" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*girlish giggle* I don't even care if his hair looks fake, I WANT HIM. <br><br>Whoa, anyway, getting off topic. *wink* <br><br>The fact that <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Maura was a lesbian <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span> was totally expected, even though Cate was all surprised. I suspected it from the beginning. <br>I liked how Jessica tied in the historical factors of the time from when this books was taking place. Girls who were even a little strange were accused of witchery and arrested, girls who liked other girls were arrested, women in general were arrested, basically. <br>But oh my god, was it SLOW. <br><br>If you like Jane Austen novels, with MORE romance, and a little bit of witchery thrown in, pick this up.<br>But if you prefer action, adventure, no kissy kissy scenes, and have a short attention span, DO NOT pick this up. <br><br>Thanks Jessica, for my signed copy. I had so much fun meeting you and listening to your advice for young authors. :)</["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<div id="review_228582548" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/228582548" />
    <a title="Minli" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/981514-minli"><img alt="Minli" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1319807416p2/981514.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/228582548?book_show_action=true">Oct 28, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Minli" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Minli" href="/user/show/981514-minli">Minli</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981514-minli?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/981514-minli?shelf=speculative">speculative</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer228582548" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10243820755444771717">This will definitely appeal to certain types of readers, but it's really not for me. Some parts were interesting, and it was compelling in the sense that it wasn't bad enough for me to give up on.<br/><br/>Cate Cahill and her two sisters, Maura and Tess, live in an alternate history 1870s New England, where a religious order called the Brotherhood extrapolates the Salem witch trial era. Except witches and magic are actually real (though quite rare, so we're told), and if they're caught, the Brotherhood wi</span>
  <span id="freeText10243820755444771717" style="display:none">This will definitely appeal to certain types of readers, but it's really not for me. Some parts were interesting, and it was compelling in the sense that it wasn't bad enough for me to give up on.<br /><br />Cate Cahill and her two sisters, Maura and Tess, live in an alternate history 1870s New England, where a religious order called the Brotherhood extrapolates the Salem witch trial era. Except witches and magic are actually real (though quite rare, so we're told), and if they're caught, the Brotherhood will sentence them to hard labour or an insane asylum. Abandoned by their father and with their mother dead, Cate and her sisters are developing a reputation in the town for being bluestockings. One day, Cate discovers a family secret while reading her mother's diary--a prophecy made over a century ago, which states that a horrible fate hinges on three sisters all being witches having the power to destroy the current social order. So, duh, everyone thinks it's the Cahill sisters, including the Brotherhood.<br /><br />Now, I'm all for religious inquisitions. I loved Elizabeth Bunce's <i>Star Crossed</i>, for instance. It's basically a historical version of the current crop of dystopian fiction out there. Your entire life is regimented by the big bad controlling authority and you live in constant fear of being discovered. But this one just made no fucking sense whatsoever. I'm told witches are rare, and then BOOM, it turns out the Sisterhood (which runs concurrently to the Brotherhood and is full of nonmarried women) is FULL OF WITCHES and they've all managed to keep this a secret from HALF the population. The magic system is hokey at best and damned stupid at worst--basically a copy of faux Latin "spells" that without any of the whimsy of Harry Potter. <br /><br />The marketing copy calls this lush prose, but I found some parts stilted and awkward, especially the beginning. I know this book wanted to be a book about sisters and how women are stifled in society, but the most interesting thing about it was the romance. I actually really liked Finn, the male romantic lead, and Cate's chemistry with him was undeniable. <br /><br />Ultimately, this book is too angsty for me. And the cover makes it look sooo trashy. </span>
  <a data-text-id="10243820755444771717" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_154697489" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154697489" />
    <a title="Krystle" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle"><img alt="Krystle" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1403921272p2/2639204.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154697489?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Krystle" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Krystle" href="/user/show/2639204-krystle">Krystle</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2639204-krystle?shelf=did-not-finish">did-not-finish</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154697489" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4475545873421812181">I tried so hard to finish this book but after chapter five this became an exercise in withstanding torture. The pacing of this book is ridiculously slow. I swear, I would read one page and start searching for something else to do.<br/><br/>The problem stems from the main character, Cate. She is such a dull sponge - one that'll suck all the fun out of life. There is no vibrancy to her, no spark. She is completely devoid of anything that incites excitement or empathy in me. She's also extremely passive, pre</span>
  <span id="freeText4475545873421812181" style="display:none">I tried so hard to finish this book but after chapter five this became an exercise in withstanding torture. The pacing of this book is ridiculously slow. I swear, I would read one page and start searching for something else to do.<br /><br />The problem stems from the main character, Cate. She is such a dull sponge - one that'll suck all the fun out of life. There is no vibrancy to her, no spark. She is completely devoid of anything that incites excitement or empathy in me. She's also extremely passive, preferring to keep things to herself even though she likes to complain about her pains excessively internally. She's too scared to speak up or even say something contrary. Sure a lot of this is bred from the environment she's raised in but really. Show at least some energy. Another thing? I've only read to slightly less than the halfway mark but I can already tell this is going to devolve into some crappy love triangle fest that'll have me gnashing my teeth.<br /><br />So, she's unhappy about having to marry someone and the person who IS interested in her hand is one of her old best friends who's come back from schooling. Cate, of course, dislikes this dictation of her life but he has been nothing but friendly to her since he's back and she could do a whole lot worse but then rages and grumbles about this in her thoughts but does she indicate she's unhappy about this to him? NO. She's such a faker. She smiles, is pleasant, and practically flirts with him when she's alone with him and disparages him in private. PLEASE. I hate these kind of people.<br /><br />Then we have Finn and he's the low status boy who is their gardener. There's nothing really bad about him other than he's such a FLAT character. There is no depth to him other than his red hair, dimples, and pretty smiles. Oh and did I mention he's handsome? Yeah, he is. We get that EVERY TIME Cate converses or interacts with him. She always has to bring up how she suddenly found him so handsome. Blah, blah, blah. SHUT UP, WOMAN. I know you're stuck in your own propriety rules and want to jump him so bad but I don't need to be reminded of this EVERY TIME Finn appears on the page. This is totally some heavy handed way of showing that he's the CHOSEN MAN of the triangle in bright flashing neon letters. Gross.<br /><br />I mean, the surface aspects of the world building was developed and this whole society that's very suffocating, oppressive, and demeaning on both women and magic users is pretty scary BUT the other parts do not add up. How do we get New London or Dubai? What is so different about them and how were they developed? Why is Dubai such a special place that everyone wants to go to? None of this is EVER explained (it could be later but I doubt it). <br /><br />This is such a boring addition to the YA genre. Composed of so many similar and overly used elements but, sadly, other books probably have and did do it better. <br /><br />Skip this, forealz.</span>
  <a data-text-id="4475545873421812181" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer10547765703695128749">❖ [<a href='http://youtube.com/c/WishFulfillment' rel='nofollow noopener'>booktube</a> wish fulfillment] ❖ [<a href='http://twitter.com/exsixtwosix' rel='nofollow noopener'>twitter</a> exsixtwosix] ❖<br/><br/>2020: 5 stars<br/>Very heavy-handed with the feminism and commentary about misogyny but I love that and it warmed my heart and soothed my soul.   <span id="freeText10547765703695128749" style="display:none">❖ [<a href="http://youtube.com/c/WishFulfillment" rel="nofollow noopener">booktube</a> wish fulfillment] ❖ [<a href="http://twitter.com/exsixtwosix" rel="nofollow noopener">twitter</a> exsixtwosix] ❖<br /><br />2020: 5 stars<br />Very heavy-handed with the feminism and commentary about misogyny but I love that and it warmed my heart and soothed my soul. I raised my rating since I was able to read it twice. So sad the sequels aren’t on audio. Love the protag and her sisters and the whole damn story. Still recommend!<br /><br />2017: 4 stars<br /><b>Why I Recommend Bumping This UP On Your TBR:</b> I thought women were represented well, as we're shown very different women making very different (sometimes opposing) decisions. The differences in moral codes made for interesting and a wide range of character types and made the characters and world more believable. I appreciated how the narrative continued to normalize same-sex relationships (and then we find out that her sister Elena is a lesbian). I appreciated the inclusion of and growing importance of a Japanese character and her family (though I am not Japanese so I can't speak to whether she was represented well or not and have not yet found an ownvoices review). This was immersive so I would especially recommend it to "escapism" readers. I enjoyed reading it and am looking forward to the sequel.<br /><br /><b>Why You Might Bump This Down On Your TBR:</b> All of the antagonists were described as fat and fatness was implied to be a negative character trait (aka the author very clearly is struggling with some fatphobia). <br /><br /><b>Depending On Your Personal Preferences:</b> The story progression doesn't follow a typical formula, it reads more "realistic" and unplanned (almost like the author didn't have an established outline/timeline, which I don't know if she did or not). I think this will work for some readers and will not work for others. There is a lot of filler and not a lot of action. The book felt like a very long introduction setting us up, hopefully, for action in the second.</span>

<div id="review_760886971" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/760886971" />
    <a title="Stephanie (Bookfever)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4939266-stephanie-bookfever"><img alt="Stephanie (Bookfever)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1595589358p2/4939266.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/760886971?book_show_action=true">Nov 09, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Stephanie (Bookfever)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Stephanie (Bookfever)" href="/user/show/4939266-stephanie-bookfever">Stephanie (Bookfever)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780142421871" href="/book/show/13590839-born-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=2013-publication">2013-publication</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=book-boyfriends">book-boyfriends</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=paranormal">paranormal</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4939266-stephanie-bookfever?shelf=buddy-read">buddy-read</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer760886971" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12891237549213120337">Born Wicked was a perfect example of a book that has both good as bad qualities to it. I really did like the book but in the end it wasn't enough to make me love it. This review will be a little different from my usual reviews because there was 50% of good stuff and 50% of bad stuff, in my opinion.<br/><br/><b>
  <u>The good:</u>
</b><br/><br/><b>The setting</b> - I absolutely loved the setting. I think it may be the best part of the book. I didn't actually know this book was historical until I started reading it. It's actually an alte</span>
  <span id="freeText12891237549213120337" style="display:none">Born Wicked was a perfect example of a book that has both good as bad qualities to it. I really did like the book but in the end it wasn't enough to make me love it. This review will be a little different from my usual reviews because there was 50% of good stuff and 50% of bad stuff, in my opinion.<br /><br /><b>
  <u>The good:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>The setting</b> - I absolutely loved the setting. I think it may be the best part of the book. I didn't actually know this book was historical until I started reading it. It's actually an alternate history, which made me love the setting even more. In this history it's well known that there are witches around and the brotherhood is hunting them, looking especially for three sister witches. One of these sisters is supposed to be the most powerful witch to have been born according to a prophecy. <br /><br /><b>Finn</b> - He was one of my favorite characters. He was just really cute and although I wasn't a fan of Cate, I did want them to end up together even though I think he can do much better than Cate. But anyway, he was a great character and I honestly wanted to read more about him. He brought a smile on my face whenever he was around. AND he actually has a bookstore, with his mother, that he works in after his father passed away. <br /><br /><b>Tess</b> - She was probably my favorite character in the book. She's Cate's 12 y/o sister and I just wish I had a sister like her. She was a joy to read about. She loves baking and she loves books. I honestly wish she was the main character in this book because I liked reading about her way more than I did about Cate. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The bad:</u>
</b><br /><br /><b>Cate</b> - Cate, Cate, Cate... where do I start with her? I disliked her from pretty much the beginning. She just didn't feel like a nice person at all. Sure, she loves her sisters and she's doing everything she can to protect them, as anyone would but honestly? She should've let them practice more magic in case the brotherhood would come for them. Her 15 y/o sister pointed out once how Cate never listens to her and I agree with Maura, she doesn't really listen to her sister even though I can tell she loves them very much. All Cate did was judge other people when she should've looked at herself first. And then there was the romance. I love Finn, I really really do but I didn't like how Cate suddenly fell in love with him so fast. She's known him for years but now suddenly these feelings come, right when her old childhood friend Paul returns to court Cate. Hmm... And also Cate was so judgy about using her sisters using magic while she does it a few times herself. I just hope she'll make better decisions in the next book.<br /><br /><b>Elena</b> - I wasn't sure what to think about Elena. At first I thought she wasn't so bad but after a little while I was ready for her to go. I didn't like how she led on Cate sister, Maura because I actually liked Maura, even though she does and says some questionable things too but I understand it. Yeah, I really disliked Elena. I don't think she liked hurting Maura's feelings but she did it so that deserves a slap to the face from me.<br /><br /><b>Lack of magic</b> - For a book that's supposed to be about magic there wasn't much of it. I wanted to see more spells from Cate, Maura and Tess. I really think Tess would be a fantastic witch if only Cate would let her. But anyway, yeah needed more magic. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>Overall:</u>
</b><br /><br />So this book has a bit of good and bad. There's also the Brotherhood and Sisterhood. I'm full on hating the Brotherhood for hunting witches and supressing women. But the Sisterhood sure can give them a run for their money. Just like with Elena I didn't think they're so bad at the beginning, especially when it's clear they're all witches but turns out they're also pretty insane. I obviously hated them but I didn't count the Brotherhood and Sisterhood with "the bad" part of this review because as far as bad guys go they're pretty villainous both in their own ways. And a good book just sometimes needs villains, you know.<br /><br />All in all, Born Wicked by Jessica Spotswood was a pretty quick read that had good as well as bad elements to it and the writing wasn't too shabby either + it was a fun buddy read with Jennifer from Book Bird Reviews!</span>
  <a data-text-id="12891237549213120337" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3431708-hannah?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3431708-hannah?shelf=2015-oct-2016-oct">2015-oct-2016-oct</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1288342430" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14547411441769178220"><a href='http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.de/2015/11/review-born-wicked-by-jessica-spotswood.html' rel='nofollow noopener'>MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br/><br/>Okay so I had my eye on this series for some time now. I was not sure about it but when our bookshop announced 16% sale I could not just ignore the fact that I wanted to read this book. And no, ebook was not enough for me! I love witches and I want them all on my shelf!<br/><br/>THE WORLD: Oh it is so different to what we are used to. So once upon a time New England was the place ruled by witches. But they abused their power and then normal people killed them. The Broth</span>
  <span id="freeText14547411441769178220" style="display:none"><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.de/2015/11/review-born-wicked-by-jessica-spotswood.html" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a><br /><br />Okay so I had my eye on this series for some time now. I was not sure about it but when our bookshop announced 16% sale I could not just ignore the fact that I wanted to read this book. And no, ebook was not enough for me! I love witches and I want them all on my shelf!<br /><br />THE WORLD: Oh it is so different to what we are used to. So once upon a time New England was the place ruled by witches. But they abused their power and then normal people killed them. The Brotherhood came of power. What it means? It means that Brotherhood controls everything, that men are in power and much better than women. The job of women is to serve the husband and not have her own opinion. If you do not like it you are eliminated from the society. Men are better and you submit to them. It is funny to read about how Brother teaches women in the Sunday service that they should not enjoy the kiss because it is a sin, how they should not read books because it is not for their mind to understand. Every women is a wicked lustful creature but it is the way she was born and the Lord forgives her, therefore she must do everything what her husband says and not ever be of her own mind. When the girl is 17 she is married or goes to Sisterhood. If she has not found a husband by then the Brotherhood will find it for her. It is crazy I am telling you, so many times I was just crazy mad but I think that is what makes this book interesting, the world is too absurd not to get involved!<br /><br />CHARACTERS: This book really is about three sisters who are also witches. The oldest Cate is of the center figure so far. She has made a promise to her mother to protect Maura and Tess, her younger sisters. You know this kind of sacrificing characters who do everything for others? Usually I hate them. But Cate is rather lovable. I really liked the way she grew as a character. Maura on the other hand, oh how she annoys me! Little brat! But Tess...the cute little pie! She is so absolutely adorable!<br />Then we have a missing father figure as always and a noisy neighbor. Additionally, the governess Elena comes to prepare the girls for the womanhood as their mother died a few years ago. I had a feeling about Elena from the beginning to be honest, somehow in this book I was always on Cate's side, it was easy to feel what she was feeling!<br /><br />LOVE: Okay so in this book we have two men but nope, no love triangle! Paul comes back to marry Cate but does Cate want to marry him? Noooo! She has no real feeling towards him whatsoever! And good because Finn...oh how can you not love him? I am shipping oh so shipping him and Cate!<br /><br />PLUS: This book really makes you feel a lot! But what I loved the most was how magic and witchery was presented. It was not what I expected but I liked it nevertheless. Plus, the bookshop chapters...mmmm.<br /><br />MINUS: I think when I went into this book I sorta was looking for Manon from the Throne of Glass type of character. I did not find it. Also, in the beginning like most of the new series it was rather slow for me. But oh well, not every book is the same, right? So it really is juts tiny thing, I lowered my expectations a little bit and loved the book alright!<br /><br /><br /><a href="http://psilovethatbook.blogspot.de/2015/11/review-born-wicked-by-jessica-spotswood.html" rel="nofollow noopener">MORE? MORE! @ P.S. I love that book!</a></span>
