<div id="review_154703424" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154703424" />
    <a title="Nafiza" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza"><img alt="Nafiza" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1529831446p2/2483439.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154703424?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Nafiza" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Nafiza" href="/user/show/2483439-nafiza">Nafiza</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2483439-nafiza?shelf=read-2012">read-2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154703424" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3404453240022885506">Dear Cate,<br/><br/>Let's talk, you and me. We're both women, we'll definitely have no problem finding at least one topic to find common ground in. We started off as friends, you and I. I quite understood and empathized with the horror you felt concerning the chauvinistic bastards who organized themselves as the Brotherhood and whose main aim was to ensure that women did not move out of their place in the supposed "natural" order of things. I was quite disgusted and I dare say, felt your anger at the crim</span>
  <span id="freeText3404453240022885506" style="display:none">Dear Cate,<br /><br />Let's talk, you and me. We're both women, we'll definitely have no problem finding at least one topic to find common ground in. We started off as friends, you and I. I quite understood and empathized with the horror you felt concerning the chauvinistic bastards who organized themselves as the Brotherhood and whose main aim was to ensure that women did not move out of their place in the supposed "natural" order of things. I was quite disgusted and I dare say, felt your anger at the crimes constantly perpetrated against women. I felt your pain as you tried to be a mother to your sisters, one of whom needed a good slap that you managed to restrain yourself from giving. And the freedom of the Arab girls? So clever. I enjoyed a chuckle though I don't know if that was what was intended. Anyway, we were good friends.<br /><br />Until you started being annoying. This was due to two main things. Two main people. Two boys. I feel bad for Paul. I really do. First there is a flashback where I am led to believe that Paul holds more meaning to you than he apparently does. My bad. His arrival is heralded with a lot of fanfare and anticipation and I thought I'd hold your hand and squeal as your heart palpitated. I guess not. Of course he's handsome and totally in love with you despite other girls wanting him oh so badly. Unfortunately, you have a thing for the gardener. Finn. Who seems perfectly nice but if you have a thing for him, why the heck do you lead on Paul? Why do you promise not to marry anyone else, explicitly mind you, and then in the next chapter, you are oh so blithely agreeing to marry Finn. Why do you do that, Cate? That's not cool. This "best friend" of yours, Paul, surely deserves more than the shoddy treatment you insist on giving him.<br /><br />But Cate, I think our relationship failed entirely when you continued not doing anything even in the face of annihilation. What is the point, I ask you, of having so much power when you are standing there, doing nothing and waiting for the bad guys to win. And the Sisterhood? Psht. I actually admire them more than I admire you. At least they use the agency they have to do shit that is actually bigger than them. You are selfish, Cate, and the ending is supposed to make me empathize with you? It didn't. It just made me roll my eyes a lot more at the insistence on pathos in a series that really could have been organized into something that flowed on its own. Because Cate, as you waffle and wibble about true love and all the sacrifices you are making, you are being <i>forced</i> to make, there are other girls, some even the ages of your own sisters, who are being killed, yes Cate, that means not alive anymore, while you bemoan the fact that you have to actually think beyond yourself. Yes, I realize there's no one as important as you are, not even the two unlikely witches who mind you are cooler than you, but when you are the heroine of a novel, you gotta do shit to be shit, like say, I dunno, Katniss does for Primrose? If you had to be Katniss, you'd never volunteer because what if that vixen to whom you sell beavers (or something) stole Gale while you were away fighting for your life? So for all the proselytizing you do about doing anything (ANYTHING) for your sisters, you don't actually do anything. You are <i>forced</i> to which is a markedly different from volunteering to. So Cate, you fail.<br /><br />And that's why, Cate, you and I part ways and I don't think we are ever going to resurrect our relationship. It's a shame but I did so enjoy the pretty cover you appeared in. Here's hoping you grow some balls in the sequels. Not that I'll be around to witness it.<br /><br />Sincerely,<br />Nafiza.</span>

<div id="review_178787642" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/178787642" />
    <a title="Sarah Mac" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac"><img alt="Sarah Mac" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1499925811p2/4490376.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/178787642?book_show_action=true">Jun 22, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Mac" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Mac" href="/user/show/4490376-sarah-mac">Sarah Mac</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-2012">zzz-2012</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=read-regifted">read-regifted</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-departed-4-star-not-keeper">zzz-departed-4-star-not-keeper</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=reviewed">reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4490376-sarah-mac?shelf=zzz-departed-ya">zzz-departed-ya</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer178787642" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2580728605304054048">When I found this among a pile of early releases at work, I chalked it up to destiny. Thanks to a crappy YA track record, my grabbing <i>Born Wicked</i> was akin to a 30-day trial on a steamer from HSN. It might explode in my face, but I could still mail that sucker back -- no money lost, just the fleshy bit of my cheek & one eyebrow.<br/><br/>Looking past the lovely cover, the first thing I noticed was first-person present tense. *sigh* (Authors of the world, PLEASE stop using present tense in teen fiction.) Fu</span>
  <span id="freeText2580728605304054048" style="display:none">When I found this among a pile of early releases at work, I chalked it up to destiny. Thanks to a crappy YA track record, my grabbing <i>Born Wicked</i> was akin to a 30-day trial on a steamer from HSN. It might explode in my face, but I could still mail that sucker back -- no money lost, just the fleshy bit of my cheek &amp; one eyebrow.<br /><br />Looking past the lovely cover, the first thing I noticed was first-person present tense. *sigh* (Authors of the world, PLEASE stop using present tense in teen fiction.) Full disclosure: I consider present tense to be a hurdle that the story must overcome. (What can I say. If you're going to be 'avant garde' enough to forgo the fundamental, ease-of-reading basic known as Past Tense Narrative, at <i>minimum</i> I demand that your choice doesn't interfere with my enjoyment.) So while I don't approve in general, I will say this much -- the present tense in <i>Born Wicked</i> was decent enough. Cate does have a serious bent of mind, which might bother some readers -- and yes, at times she can be overbearing &amp; judgemental. I didn't mind that. Given world-building circumstances, I'd have been more critical if she <i>wasn't</i> high-minded &amp; distrustful.<br /><br />Cate &amp; her sisters live in an alternate New England, a turn-of-the-century wherein the USA is cobbled together from various regions under cultural influence of various countries &amp; societies. In the case of New England, what originally began as a society dedicated to religious freedom has been overthrown by a strict patriarchal leadership known as The Brotherhood. These guys frown on all things cheerful &amp; frivolous, bur their primary goal is to stamp out witchcraft in any form. Why? Because witchcraft empowers women, &amp; women in power are abusive, power-hungry tramps who use magic to warp minds &amp; screw with masculine authority. They're also determined to find the source of a very specific prophecy which predicts the fall of the Brotherhood &amp; the re-rise of the Sisterhood (a coven disguised as the Brotherhood's female counterpart).<br /><br />Cate resents having to hide her magic &amp; feign a docile attitude toward males everywhere. But when her father arranges for a governess to join the household, suddenly the Brotherhood &amp; the Sisterhood are both poking at the Cahill family -- monitoring their trips in town, watching what they read &amp; who they socialize with, trying determine if she &amp; her sisters are the girls of prophecy -- and each institution threatens to destroy their facade of normality. Cate would as soon be left entirely alone, though her sisters are more open to magic...and, of course, she's drawn to an entirely unsuitable beau. (N.B.: there is a mild love triangle, but it wasn't obnoxious or unbelievable.) Cate worries about growing close to another family who's so subtly subversive toward the Brotherhood -- but when she &amp; Finn hatch a plan to be together, they're thwarted by some rather interesting revelations about the witch/not-witch ratio in their backwater town. <br /><br />I wager there will be a HEA at the close of the series. That being said, it's nice to read a teenage heroine capable of disassociating from her lust &amp; making a self-sacrifice a positive trait, not just a necessary evil to achieve her never-in-doubt victories. Despite a genuinely smothered lifestyle &amp; surroundings, she manages to find ways to be strong that ring true to her circumstances -- and that's more than I can say for the majority of YA heroines.</span>
  <a data-text-id="2580728605304054048" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/38613526-steffi-au-penguinbooks?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>

<span id="freeTextContainer910845278718562990"><i>“Reading is the perfect escape from whatever ails you.”</i><br/><br/>Well, I expected way more of this story, sadly.<br/><br/><u>What I liked:</u><br/><b>The world building</b>.   <span id="freeText910845278718562990" style="display:none"><i>“Reading is the perfect escape from whatever ails you.”</i><br /><br />Well, I expected way more of this story, sadly.<br /><br /><u>What I liked:</u><br /><b>The world building</b>. This book takes place in 1900 in New England (an alternative version) and women are ... I don't want to write pets because pets might have even more rights then women do. At times, it was really disgusting and hard for me to read about the oppression of women by the Brotherhood. <br /><br /><b>The dynamic between Cate (16), Maura (15) and Tess (12)</b>. Both normal boys, kind of boring. <br /><br /><b>Too many repitions</b>. After 30 pages I could have told you in my sleep what hair colour Maura has and that she is more beautiful than Cate and so on. Further, this book was way too long. If you expect a book about witchery and magic, I have to disappoint you. <br /><br /><b>Cate</b>. If I had the chance to have powers like Cate, I would embrace my power and use them to protect the ones I love. However, Cate hates her powers. I mean, she has the power to protect her family and to maybe save the oppressed women in this book. But well, she had to decide between Paul and Finn. That's more important ...<br /><br />I really really hope that Cate embraces her powers now and fights. And that we get more witchery, please.<br /><br /><b>3 stars</b></span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_177195611" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/177195611" />
    <a title="Steph Su" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su"><img alt="Steph Su" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1504243050p2/2010935.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/177195611?book_show_action=true">Jun 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Steph Su" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Steph Su" href="/user/show/2010935-steph-su">Steph Su</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=cover-lust">cover-lust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2010935-steph-su?shelf=debs12">debs12</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer177195611" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1966242866430393529">There’s no good way for me to start this review except to just come straight out and say that this book disappointed me. With a pretty cover and interesting premise but lacking in world-building, solid pacing, and full characterization, BORN WICKED seems to exemplify all that is characteristic of recently published YA that are big hits but technically weak. So what follows is probably going to be more of a what-not-to-do essay for YA writers, and I hope to God that future writers and publishers </span>
  <span id="freeText1966242866430393529" style="display:none">There’s no good way for me to start this review except to just come straight out and say that this book disappointed me. With a pretty cover and interesting premise but lacking in world-building, solid pacing, and full characterization, BORN WICKED seems to exemplify all that is characteristic of recently published YA that are big hits but technically weak. So what follows is probably going to be more of a what-not-to-do essay for YA writers, and I hope to God that future writers and publishers will take these points into consideration <i>before</i> publishing their books.<br /><br />So let’s begin by going down that list, I guess. BORN WICKED claims to take place in an alternate history of the world, but unless your copy of the book came with the Editor’s Note saying so, it’s extremely difficult to figure out the “rules” of said world. BORN WICKED is set in an alternate world where New England is religiously oppressed and women dream of someday going to “Dubai” and engaging in freedom of expression. All of these similarities-but-differences beg the question: so where in the course of Earth’s history did things change? Only that is never explained in the book. There is no explanation of any “turning points” that led to this alternate course of history. Instead we simply have proper nouns like Dubai and New London and Mexico and the Indo-China War with no anchors in our own history. We have details like dress shapes and vague descriptions of architecture but the details seem to be a jumbled mix of Victorian, American Colonial, and Asian history.<br /><br />Look. If you want to write a fantasy, then just make up different names and say that your inspiration came from the Salem Witch Trials. <i>Dune</i> is often said to be an allegory of the Middle East oil crisis, but it’s not set in the Middle East of our world, is it? If you want to write a story that has its roots in our world, then you damn well better explain in the story how your fictional setting came about. People seem to be confused about how to world-build different genres. For the record, science fiction, dystopian, and alternate-history settings require MORE world-building than fantasy, because they are a what-if regarding a possible different future or past track that we could take. Science fiction, dystopian, and alternate-history settings must, if anything, read like contemporary fiction: the world in the story must be completely natural for readers.<br /><br />I think I’ve said enough about that one subject. Moving on.<br /><br />Some people think it’s a good thing that the last several chapters of a 300-plus-page book are dramatic and full of startling revelations and villains going BOOM and protagonists agonizing over difficult decisions that they must make in a pinch of a moment. <i>This is not a good thing.</i> It means that the pacing is uneven and that the rest of the book up until the last few dramatic chapters either drag painfully or could have been condensed into a few chapters without losing anything. You don’t sell a 300-plus-page book by saying, oh my goodness, but just wait until you get to page 300. Page 300?! No. The <i>first</i> 300 pages need to be tight. They need to be informative. They need to ensnare the reader. The last few chapters CANNOT justify the first several hundred pages. I don’t find the last few dramatic chapters of a book to <i>ever</i> justify the amount of time I spent dragging myself through the first several hundred pages.<br /><br />And finally, characterization. Writers, minor characters deserve almost the same amount of thought and development you give to major characters. Consider that, if they were real (which is kind of the point of writing fiction: to make everything feel as real and believable as possible, no matter your intention for doing so), minor characters could and should have the potential to be protagonists of their own stories somewhere out there. All of the characters in BORN WICKED are kind of jumbled together in my mind. No one stands out. The Biggest and Baddest Villains are Completely Opaque-Black Badddd, but nearly everyone else’s natures and backstories seem to be able to be summarized in just two sentences each. If you want your characters—and thus, essentially, your story—to be memorable for readers, this is not the way to go.<br /><br />BORN WICKED is probably not better or worse than most of the other hyped YA out there, but, coming at the end of a looooong line of other hyped YA that display the same problems, it has, unfortunately, been forced to bear the brunt of my frustration with recent YA. BORN WICKED really isn’t <i>bad</i>, depending on what standards you have. If you’ve found yourself enjoying most of the YA bestsellers of the past year or so, then BORN WICKED will be your cup of tea. If you are looking for standout YA that elevate the genre, though, it may be best not to have too high expectations for this book. I’m going to get off the computer and go hit some walls now.</span>
  <a data-text-id="1966242866430393529" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_154868362" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/154868362" />
    <a title="Brodie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/2748076-brodie"><img alt="Brodie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1549082975p2/2748076.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/154868362?book_show_action=true">Mar 16, 2011</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brodie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brodie" href="/user/show/2748076-brodie">Brodie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Paperback 9780141342108" href="/book/show/13410054-born-wicked">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/2748076-brodie?shelf=2012">2012</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer154868362" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4179638953831719655">After the death of her mother, Cate Cahill had to take on the responsibility of caring for her two younger sisters. Her father is rarely home and even when he is, he's not exactly the most reliable of men. Not to mention he knows nothing of his daughters whispered spells. Only their mother knew of their magic and urged them against telling <i>anyone</i>, father included. So for years, Cate has had to act as mother more often than sister, and while they've had their many ups and downs, inviting anyone i</span>
  <span id="freeText4179638953831719655" style="display:none">After the death of her mother, Cate Cahill had to take on the responsibility of caring for her two younger sisters. Her father is rarely home and even when he is, he's not exactly the most reliable of men. Not to mention he knows nothing of his daughters whispered spells. Only their mother knew of their magic and urged them against telling <i>anyone</i>, father included. So for years, Cate has had to act as mother more often than sister, and while they've had their many ups and downs, inviting anyone into their private lives to offer help is a dangerous and unthinkable notion. So when her father hires a Governess, on the word of their nosy neighbour, to help transform the girls into ladies fit for society, Cate is more than a little apprehensive. But she only has a few months left to decide her own fate - accept the hand of an eligible man in marriage or join the Sisterhood? Because this is far removed from a time where women have access to a thing called <i>freedom</i>.<br /><br />Where Cate did her best to make sure she and her sisters flew under the radar, Maura, the middle child, felt trapped. And when a flighty spirit is suffocated, she will thrash her wings until she is freed. She's reckless and feisty, but she added flair to the story and even if there's times where you want to shake her by the shoulders, she <i>will</i> intrigue you. And I so adored Tess! Sweet and eager and a little lonely, for the youngest sister she was wise beyond her years. But even she wasn't happy to let their magic stay untapped like Cate wanted. I loved the strong bond the sisters shared. It may have been fragile at times, with Maura especially, but you could see the love was still strong underneath. Cate herself is an amazing protagonist. Not only for the responsibilities she's taken on at such a young age, but for the fierce and stubborn young spirit inside her, something that is always so invigorating to see from a girl in that historical period. She would truly shine in our modern world, but her day <i>needs </i>a girl like her. To offer hope for revolution, to punch through the stifling restrictions that are forced upon females.<br /><br />Oh <i>Finn</i>, my feathery Finn! The feather scene? One of my favourites in the book &lt;3 You might have seen the stunning moment captured in the book trailer and oh, it's even sweeter in words. Finn is the quiet, intelligent scholar; passionate about learning, with the kindest of hearts. His own loyalty to his family mirrors Cate's, and what's so beautiful is that he accepts and admires her for who she is -  in all her unladylike splendor. He's just a book keeper, taking on the additional job of gardening to try help his family out of financial unrest. He knows he can't offer Cate what Paul (her childhood friend and now suitor) can, but his heart is worth a thousand times the gold any man could give. I did sort of like Paul. He also appreciated Cate for who she was, not who he <i>expected</i> her to be, but I felt Finn was much more of the 'soulmate' type of match. Plus, Paul's behaviour toward Finn in their years at school earned him many narrowed eyes from me!<br /><br />While my heart did swoon and miss a beat throughout the book, it often thudded angrily, so <i>infuriated</i> with certain people and their rules!! I wanted to reach through and gouge their eyes out, but that would only result in a shredded book and it's too beautiful to ruin. The Brotherhood sprout their, '<i>witches are wicked, evil, unholy,</i>' rubbish upon the entire community and not adhering to their rules is basically signing your own suicide letter. They rule with an iron-clad fist and their word is absolute, so if they deem a young lady a witch, then they'll drag her away kicking and screaming until she's locked away in an asylum. Or put to death.<br /><br />The Sisterhood is Cate's second option to marriage, but it's not exactly a viable choice for Cate when it would separate her from her sisters. They're said to offer ladies the best they can in terms of skills and education, but are they perhaps hiding a few secrets of their own?<br /><br />Born Wicked is a beautifully written debut that had me under a spell from the very first page. Jessica Spotswood has such gorgeous prose. She creates deep and touching characters that you truly care for, unless they're in the Brotherhood, who you only care to stake through the heart. With breathtaking magic, haunting prophecies and impossible choices, Born Wicked is wickedly captivating. If you love romance and danger, sacrifice and magic, and your heroines brave, then this is a novel you cannot pass up!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4179638953831719655" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_510202512" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/510202512" />
    <a title="Liz" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14811808-liz"><img alt="Liz" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1585394064p2/14811808.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">

        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/510202512?book_show_action=true">Jan 18, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Liz" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Liz" href="/user/show/14811808-liz">Liz</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer963357200577512801">I love books about witches and vampires and evil creatures in general. <br/>This was another read I really enjoyed. <br/><br/>Cate, Tess and Maura are sisters. Moreover they are witches and they have to hide their abilities because the ruling Brotherhood is hunting witches down. After the death of their mother Cate has to take care of her sisters and watch over them so they are more careful with their magic. At the same time, Cate has to decide whether to join the Sisterhood or to marry and both possibilities </span>
  <span id="freeText963357200577512801" style="display:none">I love books about witches and vampires and evil creatures in general. <br />This was another read I really enjoyed. <br /><br />Cate, Tess and Maura are sisters. Moreover they are witches and they have to hide their abilities because the ruling Brotherhood is hunting witches down. After the death of their mother Cate has to take care of her sisters and watch over them so they are more careful with their magic. At the same time, Cate has to decide whether to join the Sisterhood or to marry and both possibilities are not perfect for her. Both mean that she has to leave her sisters. <br />The situation gets even more tensed when their father arranges Elena and Finn. Especially because Cate plans to marry Paul. Finn confuses her.<br />And then, there are also the two other girls of the neighborhood, Sachi and Rory and an old prophecy...<br /><br />Firstly, I really lliked the write style of this book. It reminded me on an old romantical Gothic novel and took the reader to a completely different world. <br />The plot was interesting, there were some nice turning points and surprises in it and the book was full of secrets that were wisely revealed step by step. <br />Cate is a nice character who is determined and a bit stiff but yet has a great and enjoyable humour and way of acting and thinking. She is lonely and she is strong, and the fact that she is an extremly talented witch makes her even more interesting. <br />Tess, the youngest of the sisters is a sister everybody wishes for! She is childish when she has to be and more grown up than Cate when she sees that Cate is overwhelmed. She supports and helps her sister. A reliable and sweet character I really enjoyed reading about!<br />Maura on the contrary. I couldn't stand this spoiled girl who only wanted attention. Same about Paul and Elena. <br /><br />It is indeed interesting how much the characters change during the book. Some reveal secrets, others develop and others show who they truly are. <br />This book was far away from being predictable! <br />I would recommend this book to fans of the paranormal genre</span>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer212758144" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11778723704204246726">I was lucky enough to win an arc of this from the author's blog, and wow, am I so glad I did. The prose was lush and evocative, beautifully painting the world Cate lives in. The idea of a world where women, and witches especially, are supressed by an all powerful "Brotherhood" was compelling, and the worldbuilding felt genuine. All the characters had their own personalitites and issues,and I never felt like the secondary charactors were just a backdrop to the action. The main romance of the book</span>
  <span id="freeText11778723704204246726" style="display:none">I was lucky enough to win an arc of this from the author's blog, and wow, am I so glad I did. The prose was lush and evocative, beautifully painting the world Cate lives in. The idea of a world where women, and witches especially, are supressed by an all powerful "Brotherhood" was compelling, and the worldbuilding felt genuine. All the characters had their own personalitites and issues,and I never felt like the secondary charactors were just a backdrop to the action. The main romance of the book was excellent as well- Cate and Finn are now one of my favorite book couples of all time. I also loved the family relationship between Cate, Maura, and Tess: I LOVE love love reading about siblings in ya, and I thought this was very well done. Born Wicked is way better than your average young adult paranormal, and I think even people who AREN'T normally fantasy readers could definitely enjoy it. Read it. </span>
  <a data-text-id="11778723704204246726" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1759656807" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1759656807" />
    <a title="Brigid ✩" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/886144-brigid"><img alt="Brigid ✩" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1581869052p2/886144.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1759656807?book_show_action=true">Sep 23, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brigid ✩" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brigid ✩" href="/user/show/886144-brigid">Brigid ✩</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=historical-fiction">historical-fiction</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=young-adult">young-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/886144-brigid?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1759656807" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16911590128842905251">I went into this book knowing next to nothing about it except that it involved witches––and hey, I haven't read very many books that dealt with witches/witchcraft so I was excited to give it a try! And, well, I liked it. It was a light and fun read. There are a few things I wish had been better, but overall it was enjoyable.<br/><br/><b>What I liked:</b><br/><br/>- It has an interesting, kind of "alternate history" setting which wasn't what I expected. And I love alternate histories and historical fantasy, so I liked that</span>
  <span id="freeText16911590128842905251" style="display:none">I went into this book knowing next to nothing about it except that it involved witches––and hey, I haven't read very many books that dealt with witches/witchcraft so I was excited to give it a try! And, well, I liked it. It was a light and fun read. There are a few things I wish had been better, but overall it was enjoyable.<br /><br /><b>What I liked:</b><br /><br />- It has an interesting, kind of "alternate history" setting which wasn't what I expected. And I love alternate histories and historical fantasy, so I liked that element of it. <br />- I like Cate and her sisters, and how they're so dedicated to each other. I'm always happy to see strong sister relationships in books! <br />- I really love Maura for some reason? Like... if I do end up reading the sequel(s) it will mainly be because of her (assuming there's more of her in the other books). She was definitely the most compelling character for me. <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Btw I somehow knew from the beginning that she was bi, lol. Maybe it's just me, a fellow bisexual, projecting myself onto every character, but I was like....hmmmMMM. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- The book deals with some interesting themes about gender roles, sexism, sexuality, etc. etc. which I appreciated. It could've delved into those themes a <i>little</i> more, but I was glad they were touched upon, at least. <br /><br /><b>What didn't work for me:</b><br /><br />- This isn't exactly a fast-paced book. I don't mind books taking things a little slow, but I wish it'd had a bit more of a plot. <br />- The love triangle. *frustrated sigh* You know, I actually didn't mind the romance in this book. Finn is pretty cool and he and Cate are cute together. But then there was all this stupid stuff with Paul, and I was kind of like, "....Who?" I didn't see why he was necessary to the story, and throwing him in there didn't seem to add much. I think it would've been compelling enough with Cate just being in love with Finn and not wanting him to find out she's a witch and all. I don't think there needed to be this extra subplot of "Oh no, which cute boy shall I marry?!" It only slowed things down, really. <br />- I wish there had been more magic. For a book about witches there was .... not a lot of witchcraft. There was a lot of focus on the romance and drama and whatnot, and I really just wanted to see more of Cate and her sisters testing their powers. There was more of that towards the end, so I became a little more invested––but honestly through the first half of the book or so, I kept almost forgetting that it was even a fantasy. <br /><br /><b>The final word:</b><br /><br /><b>Pros:</b><br /><br />- a quick, fun read<br />- sisterhood!<br />- <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[some bi (I guess??) representation, hell yeah <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />- some thought-provoking themes<br /><br /><b>Cons:</b><br /><br />- a bit slow-paced<br />- love triangle<br />- not enough magic<br /><br />So .... I had a couple issues with this book, but I liked it well enough that I might give the next one a try! </span>
  <a data-text-id="16911590128842905251" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_545263742" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/545263742" />
    <a title="Bern" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4789508-bern"><img alt="Bern" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1463420514p2/4789508.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/545263742?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bern" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bern" href="/user/show/4789508-bern">Bern</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=2013">2013</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=coverlust">coverlust</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=favourites">favourites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=ya">ya</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=magically-delicious">magically-delicious</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=paranormality">paranormality</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=perfection">perfection</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=the-glorious-shelf-of-fabulousness">the-glorious-shelf-of-fabulousness</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=loved-it-to-bits">loved-it-to-bits</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/4789508-bern?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer545263742" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3235463223801061711">Oh, my god.<br/><br/>Oh. My. <i>God</i>.<br/><br/>What is this book, even? I'm unable to cope with this book, I just really can't even. Look at my eloquence. I mean, I used to possess a <i>semblance</i> of it, and now look at me, all unfinished sentences and using "even" every five words or so.<br/><br/>Born Wicked is amazing. It's the kind of book that translates perfectly to images in your head and always has you on the edge of your proverbial seat, anxious to know what's coming next. I think a movie of this should be made, and then act</span>
  <span id="freeText3235463223801061711" style="display:none">Oh, my god.<br><br>Oh. My. <i>God</i>.<br><br>What is this book, even? I'm unable to cope with this book, I just really can't even. Look at my eloquence. I mean, I used to possess a <i>semblance</i> of it, and now look at me, all unfinished sentences and using "even" every five words or so.<br><br>Born Wicked is amazing. It's the kind of book that translates perfectly to images in your head and always has you on the edge of your proverbial seat, anxious to know what's coming next. I think a movie of this should be made, and then action figures based on said movie, and then a wave of miscellaneous memorabilia to go with aforementioned action figures and just...<br><br><i>Breathe.</i> I need to breathe.<br><br>I can't really put in words how much this is just the best kind of YA that includes paranormalcy that isn't lame, romance that doesn't make you want to gouge your eyes out with rusty spikes and plot that movies at a quick pace without forsaking character development. Granted, Cate, the main character, wasn't without her flaws and I wouldn't necessarily agree with all of her actions but it doesn't matter because I was so invested in everything that was happening, and no one really agrees with someone else on everything, anyway.<br><br>To make up for my lack of eloquence, I've produced a few gifs that explain basically my emotions throughout Born Wicked:<br><br>When a certain governess shows up acting like she owns the place:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411030ra/806680.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(I WILL DESTROY YOUR TACKY SANDALS, ELENA, AND TO ADD INSULT TO INJURY I SHALL WEAR THEM AS A HAT!)<br><br>When Cate and Finn kiss:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380376341ra/731145.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Literally. I died a lot during this. Shouldn't I get a certificate from the Stuntmen Guild or something? Methinks so.)<br><br>When Maura is dumb, but Lord that girl is dumb (I still like her though):<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411030ra/806681.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(Girl, you need some help in the romance department. Seriously, listen to your sister, she knows best.)<br><br>And lastly, in the end, but really all throughout the book:<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1380411030ra/806682.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>(My feels are in SHREDS. In <i>shreds</i>, literally. Ok, well, figuratively, BUT YOU GET IT).<br></span>
  <a data-text-id="3235463223801061711" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <a title="Maria (highinthebooksky)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/20688802-maria-highinthebooksky"><img alt="Maria (highinthebooksky)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1532696900p2/20688802.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Maria (highinthebooksky)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Maria (highinthebooksky)" href="/user/show/20688802-maria-highinthebooksky">Maria (highinthebooksky)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer878556431" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1400394648158147198">to be honest I had my problems getting into the story but eventually I did! and it was worth my time!<br/><br/> born wicked is a very enjoyable<br/> story with great characters and cool time setting ! <br/><br/>Cate and her sisters have a very realistic relationship which reminds me of my own relationship with my sister sometimes... <br/>I liked how the story develops through out the book bc some aspects took me by surprise and so I'm looking forward to.read the sequel as soon as possible!</span>

          </span>
        </div>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FeNHvS9pyHyUaTQ5catCqiBIgvhKwe1nAzCwyaPGJpURrC1ItjivG2/8fHL/hTw4602AzTPkXUVeyUS3TUyx7w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('s2lzXmHKNG8REUKWmRPefY2cK+N/5H4ytV42kv300uy3Jhmr+JtTCOqECt0XPaDvRpkp1gbBzhDop8LsE35Flg==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<span id="freeTextContainer4803901451595805632">Jess is the author of the historical fantasy trilogy The Cahill Witch Chronicles and the contemporary novels Wild Swans and The Last Summer of the Garrett Girls. She is the editor of the anthologies A Tyranny of Petticoats and The Radical Element, and co-editor (with Tess Sharpe) of Toil & Trouble: 15 Tales of Women & Witchcraft. Jess lives in Washington, DC, where she works for the DC Public Libr</span>
  <span id="freeText4803901451595805632" style="display:none">Jess is the author of the historical fantasy trilogy The Cahill Witch Chronicles and the contemporary novels Wild Swans and The Last Summer of the Garrett Girls. She is the editor of the anthologies A Tyranny of Petticoats and The Radical Element, and co-editor (with Tess Sharpe) of Toil &amp; Trouble: 15 Tales of Women &amp; Witchcraft. Jess lives in Washington, DC, where she works for the DC Public Library as a children’s library associate. </span>
